{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01U2VzCkHPLFVdSVeyBVHC67","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# C++ coding style\n     2→\n     3→* The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Thus all white spaces, etc.\n     4→  issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\n     5→  the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\n     6→  (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\n     7→  .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\n     8→  comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\n     9→  To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\n    10→* Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\n    11→  [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\n    12→  The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\n    13→  guidelines.\n    14→\n    15→# Repository file layout\n    16→\n    17→* Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\n    18→\n    19→# Documentation\n    20→\n    21→* If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\n    22→  Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\n    23→\n    24→# Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\n    25→\n    26→* Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\n    27→* References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\n    28→  includes both const and non-const references.\n    29→* Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\n    30→* Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\n    31→* Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\n    32→* 100 columns is the line limit.\n    33→* Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\n    34→* Smart pointers are type aliased:\n    35→  * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\n    36→  * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\n    37→  * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\n    38→  * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\n    39→* `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\n    40→  * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\n    41→  * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\n    42→* If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\n    43→  E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\n    44→  forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\n    45→  the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\n    46→  passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\n    47→* Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\n    48→  production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\n    49→  production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\n    50→  the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\n    51→  raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\n    52→  production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\n    53→  quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \"factory\").\n    54→* Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\n    55→  explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\n    56→* The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\n    57→  This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\n    58→  advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\n    59→  fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\n    60→  how to best handle this.\n    61→* The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\n    62→  In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\n    63→  please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\n    64→  which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\n    65→* API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. Use `@param` to describe\n    66→  parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\n    67→  methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\n    68→  developer discretion. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\n    69→  documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\n    70→* Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\n    71→* All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\n    72→  exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\n    73→  Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\n    74→  the top of the file.\n    75→* If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\n    76→  from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\n    77→  In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\n    78→* Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\n    79→  NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\n    80→* [Thread\n    81→  annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\n    82→  such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\n    83→  locks/mutexes.\n    84→* Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\n    85→  rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\n    86→  [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\n    87→   allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\n    88→* Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\n    89→* Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\n    90→  names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\n    91→\n    92→# Error handling\n    93→\n    94→A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\n    95→\n    96→* All error code returns should be checked.\n    97→* At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\n    98→  - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\n    99→  - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\n   100→  - Third party dependency return codes\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Thus all white spaces, etc.\n  issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\n  the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\n  (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\n  .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\n  comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\n  To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\n* Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\n  [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\n  The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\n  guidelines.\n\n# Repository file layout\n\n* Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\n\n# Documentation\n\n* If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\n  Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\n\n# Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\n\n* Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\n* References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\n  includes both const and non-const references.\n* Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\n* Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\n* Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\n* 100 columns is the line limit.\n* Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\n* Smart pointers are type aliased:\n  * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\n  * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\n  * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\n  * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\n* `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\n  * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\n  * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\n* If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\n  E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\n  forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\n  the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\n  passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\n* Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\n  production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\n  production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\n  the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\n  raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\n  production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\n  quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \"factory\").\n* Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\n  explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\n* The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\n  This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\n  advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\n  fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\n  how to best handle this.\n* The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\n  In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. Use `@param` to describe\n  parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\n  methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\n  developer discretion. There are some\n  exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\n  Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\n  the top of the file.\n* If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\n  from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\n  In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\n* Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Earlier versions will not compile because the `afunix.h` header is not available. **The recommended Windows version is equal or later than Windows 10 SDK, version 1903 (10.0.18362.1)**\n\n    Install bazelisk in the PATH using the `bazel.exe` executable name as described above in the first section.\n\n    When building Envoy, Bazel creates very long path names. One way to work around these excessive path\n    lengths is to change the output base directory for bazel to a very short root path. An example Bazel configuration\n    to help with this is to use `C:\\_eb` as the bazel base path. This and other preferences should be set up by placing\n    the following bazelrc configuration line in a system `%ProgramData%\\bazel.bazelrc` file or the individual\n    user's `%USERPROFILE%\\.bazelrc` file (rather than including it on every bazel command line):\n\n    ```\n    startup --output_base=C:/_eb\n    ```\n\n    Another option to shorten the output root for Bazel is to set the `USERNAME` environment variable in your shell\n    session to a short value. Bazel uses this value when constructing its output root path if no explicit `--output_base`\n    is set.\n\n    Bazel also creates file symlinks when building Envoy. It's strongly recommended to enable file symlink support\n    using [Bazel's instructions](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/windows.html#enable-symlink-support).\n    For other common issues, see the\n    [Using Bazel on Windows](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/windows.html) page.\n\n    > The paths in this document are given as\n    examples, make sure to verify you are using the correct paths for your environment. Also note\n    that these examples assume using a `cmd.exe` shell to set environment variables etc., be sure\n    to do the equivalent if using a different shell.\n\n    [python3](https://www.python.org/downloads/): Specifically, the Windows-native flavor distributed\n    by python.org. The POSIX flavor available via MSYS2, the Windows Store flavor and other distributions\n    will not work. Add a symlink for `python3.exe` pointing to the installed `python.exe` for Envoy scripts\n    and Bazel rules which follow POSIX python conventions. Add `pip.exe` to the PATH and install the `wheel`\n    package.\n    ```cmd\n    mklink %USERPROFILE%\\Python39\\python3.exe %USERPROFILE%\\Python39\\python.exe\n    set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\Python39;%PATH%\n    set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\Python39\\Scripts;%PATH%\n    pip install wheel\n    ```\n\n    [Build Tools for Visual Studio 2019](https://visualstudio.microsoft.com/downloads/#build-tools-for-visual-studio-2019):\n    For building with MSVC, you must install at least the VC++ workload.\n    You may alternately install the entire Visual Studio 2019 and use the Build Tools installed in that\n    package. Earlier versions of VC++ Build Tools/Visual Studio are not recommended or supported.\n    If installed in a non-standard filesystem location, be sure to set the `BAZEL_VC` environment variable\n    to the path of the VC++ package to allow Bazel to find your installation of VC++. NOTE: ensure that\n    the `link.exe` that resolves on your PATH is from VC++ Build Tools and not `/usr/bin/link.exe` from MSYS2,\n    which is determined by their relative ordering in your PATH.\n    ```cmd\n    set BAZEL_VC=%USERPROFILE%\\VSBT2019\\VC\n    set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\VSBT2019\\VC\\Tools\\MSVC\\14.26.28801\\bin\\Hostx64\\x64;%PATH%\n    ```\n\n    The Windows SDK contains header files and libraries you need when building Windows applications. Bazel always uses the latest, but you can specify a different version by setting the environment variable `BAZEL_WINSDK_FULL_VERSION`. See [bazel/windows](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/windows.html)\n\n    [MSYS2 shell](https://msys2.github.io/): Install to a path with no spaces, e.g. C:\\msys64.\n\n    Set the `BAZEL_SH` environment variable to the path of the installed MSYS2 `bash.exe`\n    executable. Additionally, setting the `MSYS2_ARG_CONV_EXCL` environment variable to a value\n    of `*` is often advisable to ensure argument parsing in the MSYS2 shell behaves as expected.\n    ```cmd\n    set PATH=%USERPROFILE%\\msys64\\usr\\bin;%PATH%\n    set BAZEL_SH=%USERPROFILE%\\msys64\\usr\\bin\\bash.exe\n    set MSYS2_ARG_CONV_EXCL=*\n    set MSYS2_PATH_TYPE=inherit\n    ```\n\n    Set the `TMPDIR` environment variable to a path usable as a temporary directory (e.g.\n    `C:\\Windows\\TEMP`), and create a directory symlink `C:\\c` to `C:\\`, so that the MSYS2\n    path `/c/Windows/TEMP` is equivalent to the Windows path `C:/Windows/TEMP`:\n    ```cmd\n    set TMPDIR=C:/Windows/TEMP\n    mklink /d C:\\c C:\\\n    ```\n\n    The TMPDIR path and MSYS2 `mktemp` command are used frequently by the `rules_foreign_cc`\n    component of Bazel as well as Envoy's test scripts, causing problems if not set to a path\n    accessible to both Windows and msys commands. [Note the `ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script\n    which builds envoy and run tests in CI creates this symlink automatically.]\n","numLines":150,"startLine":100,"totalLines":974}}}

The toolchain\nuses git hooks extensively, copying them from `support/hooks` to the `.git`\nfolder.\n\nThe commit hook checks can be skipped using the `--no-verify` flags, as\nso:\n\n```bash\ngit commit --no-verify\n```\n\nYou can also do this by adding `NO_VERIFY` to `.env`, for example:\n\n```console\n$ echo NO_VERIFY=1 >> .env\n```\n\nOr settting it in your environment:\n\n```console\n$ export NO_VERIFY=1\n```\n\n## Functionality\n\nCurrently the development support toolchain exposes two main pieces of\nfunctionality:\n\n* Automatically appending DCO signoff to the end of a commit message if it\n  doesn't exist yet. It produces more consistent\n   329→output which is not depending on your local C++ toolchain. It can also help debugging issues with RBE. See below to configure test IP versions.\n   337→\n   338→## Linking against libc++ on Linux\n   339→\n   340→To link Envoy against libc++, follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) to setup Clang+LLVM and run:\n   341→```\n   342→bazel build --config=libc++ envoy\n   343→```\n   344→\n   345→Or use our configuration with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, pass `--config=remote-clang-libc++` or\n   346→`--config=docker-clang-libc++` respectively.\n   347→\n   348→If you want to make libc++ as default, add a line `build --config=libc++` to the `user.bazelrc` file in Envoy source root.\n   349→\n   350→## Using a compiler toolchain in a non-standard location\n   351→\n   352→By setting the `CC` and `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` in the environment that Bazel executes from as\n   353→appropriate, an arbitrary compiler toolchain and standard library location can be specified. One\n   354→slight caveat is that (at the time of writing), Bazel expects the binutils in `$(dirname $CC)` to be\n   355→unprefixed, e.g. `as` instead of `x86_64-linux-gnu-as`.\n   356→\n   357→Note: this configuration currently doesn't work with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, you have to generate a\n   358→custom toolchains configuration for them. GCC >= 9 is also known to work.\n   364→Currently the CI is running with Clang 14.\n   365→\n   366→## Clang STL debug symbols\n   367→\n   368→By default Clang drops some debug symbols that are required for pretty printing to work correctly.\n   369→More information can be found [here](https://bugs.llvm.org/show_bug.cgi?id=24202). The easy solution\n   370→is to set ```--copt=-fno-limit-debug-info``` on the CLI or in your .bazelrc file.\n   371→\n   372→## Removing debug info\n   373→\n   374→If you don't want your debug or release binaries to contain debug info\n   375→to reduce binary size, pass `--define=no_debug_info=1` when building.\n   376→This is primarily useful when building envoy as a static library. Add `-c opt` for an optimized release build or\n   `-c dbg` for an unoptimized, fully instrumented debugging build.\n\n## Building Envoy with the CI Docker image\n\nEnvoy can also be built with the Docker image used for CI, by installing Docker and executing the following.\n\nOn Linux, run:\n\n```\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\nFrom a Windows host with Docker installed, the Windows containers feature enabled, and bash (installed via\nMSYS2 or Git bash), run:\n\n**Note: the command below executes the whole Windows CI and unlike Linux you are not able to set specific build targets. You can modify `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to modify `bazel` arguments, tests to run, etc. as well as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment.**\n\n```\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\n```\n\nSee also the [documentation](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/ci) for developer use of the\nCI Docker image.\n\n## Building Envoy with Remote Execution\n\nEnvoy can also be built with Bazel [Remote Execution](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/remote-execution.html),\npart of the CI is running with the hosted [GCP RBE](https://blog.bazel.build/2018/10/05/remote-build-execution.html) service.\n\nTo build Envoy with a remote build services, run Bazel with your remote build service flags and with `--config=remote-clang`.\nFor example the following command runs build with the GCP RBE service used in CI:\n\n```\nbazel build envoy --config=remote-clang \\\n    --remote_cache=grpcs://remotebuildexecution.googleapis.com \\\n    --remote_executor=grpcs://remotebuildexecution.googleapis.com \\\n    --remote_instance_name=projects/envoy-ci/instances/default_instance\n```\n\nChange the value of `--remote_cache`, `--remote_executor` and `--remote_instance_name` for your remote build services. Tests can\nbe run in remote execution too.\n\nNote: Currently the test run configuration in `.bazelrc` doesn't download test binaries and test logs,\nto override the behavior set [`--remote_download_outputs`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html#flag--remote_download_outputs)\naccordingly.\n\n## Building Envoy with Docker sandbox\n\nBuilding Envoy with Docker sandbox uses the same Docker image used in CI with fixed C++ toolchain configuration. It produces more consistent\noutput which is not depending on your local C++ toolchain. It can also help debugging issues with RBE. To build Envoy with Docker sandbox:\n\n```\nbazel build envoy --config=docker-clang\n```\n\nTests can be run in docker sandbox too. Note that the network environment, such as IPv6, may be different in the docker sandbox so you may want\nset different options. See below to configure test IP versions.\n\n## Linking against libc++ on Linux\n\nTo link Envoy against libc++, follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) to setup Clang+LLVM and run:\n```\nbazel build --config=libc++ envoy\n```\n\nOr use our configuration with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, pass `--config=remote-clang-libc++` or\n`--config=docker-clang-libc++` respectively.\n\nIf you want to make libc++ as default, add a line `build --config=libc++` to the `user.bazelrc` file in Envoy source root.\n\n## Using a compiler toolchain in a non-standard location\n\nBy setting the `CC` and `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` in the environment that Bazel executes from as\nappropriate, an arbitrary compiler toolchain and standard library location can be specified. One\nslight caveat is that (at the time of writing), Bazel expects the binutils in `$(dirname $CC)` to be\nunprefixed, e.g. `as` instead of `x86_64-linux-gnu-as`.\n\nNote: this configuration currently doesn't work with Remote Execution or Docker sandbox, you have to generate a\ncustom toolchains configuration for them. See [bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazel-toolchains)\nfor more details.\n\n## Supported compiler versions\n\nWe now require Clang >= 9 due to C++17 support and tcmalloc requirement. GCC >= 9 is also known to work.\nCurrently the CI is running with Clang 14.\n\n## Clang STL debug symbols\n\nBy default Clang drops some debug symbols that are required for pretty printing to work correctly.\nMore information can be found [here](https://bugs.llvm.org/show_bug.cgi?id=24202). The easy solution\nis to set ```--copt=-fno-limit-debug-info``` on the CLI or in your .bazelrc file.\n\n## Removing debug info\n\nIf you don't want your debug or release binaries to contain debug info\nto reduce binary size, pass `--define=no_debug_info=1` when building.\nThis is primarily useful when building envoy as a static library. When\nbuilding a linked envoy binary you can build the implicit `.stripped`\ntarget from [`cc_binary`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/be/c-cpp.html#cc_binary)\nor pass [`--strip=always`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html#flag--strip)\ninstead.\n\n# Running the built Envoy binary on the host system\n\nAfter Envoy is built, it can be executed via CLI.\n\nFor example, if Envoy was built using the `bazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static` command, then it can be executed from the project's root directory by running:\n\n```console\n$(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy-static --config-path /path/to/your/envoy/config.yaml\n```\n\n# Testing Envoy with Bazel\n\nAll the Envoy tests can be built and run with:\n\n```\nbazel test //test/...\n```\n","numLines":150,"startLine":250,"totalLines":974}}}

In IPv4 or IPv6 only\nenvironments, set the environment variable ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS to \"v4only\" or\n\"v6only\", respectively.\n\n```\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v4only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v6only\n```\n\nBy default, tests are run with the [gperftools](https://github.com/gperftools/gperftools) heap\nchecker enabled in \"normal\" mode to detect leaks. For other mode options, see the gperftools\nheap checker [documentation](https://gperftools.github.io/gperftools/heap_checker.html). To force it to rerun tests:\n\n```\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --cache_test_results=no\n```\n\nBazel will by default run all tests inside a sandbox, which disallows access to the\nlocal filesystem. If you need to break out of the sandbox (for example to run under a\nlocal script or tool with [`--run_under`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/user-manual.html#flag--run_under)),\nyou can run the test with `--strategy=TestRunner=local`, e.g.:\n\n```\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --strategy=TestRunner=local --run_under=/some/path/foobar.sh\n```\n# Stack trace symbol resolution\n\nEnvoy can produce backtraces on demand and from assertions and other fatal\nactions like segfaults. Where supported, stack traces will contain resolved\nsymbols, though not include line numbers. On systems where absl::Symbolization is\nnot supported, the stack traces written in the log or to stderr contain addresses rather\nthan resolved symbols. If the symbols were resolved, the address is also included at\nthe end of the line.\n\nThe `tools/stack_decode.py` script exists to process the output and do additional symbol\nresolution including file names and line numbers. It requires the `addr2line` program be\ninstalled and in your path. Any log lines not relevant to the backtrace capability are\npassed through the script unchanged (it acts like a filter). File and line information\nis appended to the stack trace lines.\n\nThe script runs in one of two modes. To process log input from stdin, pass `-s` as the first\nargument, followed by the executable file path. You can postprocess a log or pipe the output\nof an Envoy process. If you do not specify the `-s` argument it runs the arguments as a child\nprocess. This enables you to run a test with backtrace post processing. Bazel sandboxing must\nbe disabled by specifying local execution. Example command line with\n`run_under`:\n\n```\nbazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test\n--run_under=//tools:stack_decode --strategy=TestRunner=local\n--cache_test_results=no --test_output=all\n```\n\nExample using input on stdin:\n\n```\nbazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test --cache_test_results=no --test_output=streamed |& tools/stack_decode.py -s bazel-bin/test/server/backtrace_test\n```\n\nYou will need to use either a `dbg` build type or the `opt` build type to get file and line\nsymbol information in the binaries.\n\nBy default main.cc will install signal handlers to print backtraces at the\nlocation where a fatal signal occurred. The signal handler will re-raise the\nfatal signal with the default handler so a core file will still be dumped after\nthe stack trace is logged. To inhibit this behavior use\n`--define=signal_trace=disabled` on the Bazel command line. No signal handlers will\nbe installed.\n\n# Running a single Bazel test under GDB\n\n```\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\ngdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\n```\n\nWe need to use `-c dbg` Bazel option to generate debugging symbols and without\nthat GDB will not be very useful. The debugging symbols are stored as separate\ndebugging information files (`.dwp` files) and we can build a DWARF package file\nwith `.dwp ` target. The `.dwp` file need to be presented in the same folder with the\nbinary for a full debugging experience.\n\n# Running Bazel tests requiring privileges\n\nSome tests may require privileges (e.g. CAP_NET_ADMIN) in order to execute. One option is to run\nthem with elevated privileges, e.g. `sudo test`. However, that may not always be possible,\nparticularly if the test needs to run in a CI pipeline. `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh` may be used in\nsuch situations to run the tests in a privileged docker container.\n\nThe script works by wrapping the test execution in the current repository's circle ci build\ncontainer, then executing it either locally or on a remote docker container. latest request and restarts them if they are\n   128→failed or cancelled.\n   129→\n   130→Links on the request page link to the original checks, but the checks themselves will\n   131→offer a and run the CI at that point.\n   138→\n   139→This means that the CI on `main` should always be able to run the current supported branches.\n   140→\n   141→There are possible workaround for custom branch CI but the better path is to ensure legacy support\n   142→in current `main` or backport any required changes.\n   143→\n   144→## CI caching\n   145→\n   146→Currently only x86 Docker images are cached.\n   147→\n   148→Github has a hard per-repo limit of 10GB cache for CI which is LRU cycled when exceeded.\n   149→\n   150→This should just be enough to store x86 and arm Docker images for most of our release branches\n   151→but will not leave anything to spare.\n   152→\n   153→We can probably set up a bucket cache for bazel and other caching but this will need to be\n   154→done to be run in non-`envoyproxy/envoy` repos\n   179→\n   180→With these flags activated the CI runs will respect the normal conditions for running.\n   181→\n   182→### CI override vars\n   183→\n No other configuration\nis read from the pull request itself.\n\n### Checks\n\nWhich checks should run against a commit or PR is configured under the `checks` key.\n\nThe names of these checks should match any checks that are set to required for the repo,\nand if a check is required this should be set in the config to ensure the check is marked\nas skipped if the related runs are skipped.\n\n### Runs\n\nThis controls which workflows run, and where necessary which jobs in the workflows.\n\nThis paths can be configured with glob matches to match changed files.\n\nPaths are always matched for PRs.\n\nFor push requests the config can be set to:\n\n- always (default): Always runs\n- paths: Runs when paths match\n- never: Doesnt run on pushes\n\n## CI requests\n\n### All CI is requested\n\nWhether triggered by push event or a pull_request all CI should be viewed as \"requested\".\n\nThis is very important as it means we can treat incoming triggers in much the same way\nas we might handle an incoming web request.\n\nMuch like a web request, CI requests may be \"trusted\" or \"untrusted\" and as a consequence\nhave more or less capability or access.\n\nAgain, much like web requests, CI requests cannot be assumed to be safe.\n\nAny incoming data - critically data over which a user has the capability to change should\nbe treated in the same way that user data is handled in a web request.\n\nFailure to do this opens our CI up to many of the same attacks you might expect in a web scenario\n- mostly injection attacks of various sorts.\n\n### Requests are always made _from_ the triggering branch\n\nThe only CI workflow that is required/used on any branch other than `main` is `request.yml`.\n\nThis file contains any custom configurations required by the branch - for example, build images.\n\nThe request workflow on any branch always delegates to the `_request.yml` on `main`.\n\nThe `_request.yml` workflow contains all required configuration for handling an incoming request.\n\nAll other CI listens for the request workflow to run, and then runs with the requested/parsed data.\n\n### CI is always run _in_ the context of main\n\nOther than updating configurations in any given `request.yml` - no CI workflows are parsed\nanywhere other than in the context of `main`.\n\nThis means that **all** changes must be made to the `main` workflows for _any_ branch _and_ for PRs.\n\nLike branch CI, PRs also run in the context of `main` - making changes to these files in a PR will have\nno effect until/unless they are landed on the `main` branch.\n\n### Lifecycle of a CI request\n\n#### Incoming request:\n\nRequests can be triggered by a  `push` to `main` or a release branch or from a\n`pull_request_target` to those branches.\n\nThe `request.yml` file handles this and *must* live on every branch.\n\nThis wf then calls the reusable `_request.yml` workflow, typically on `main`, but\nbranches can pin this if required.\n\n#### Request is handled by `_request.yml` workflow:\n\nThis workflow initially reads the `.github/config.yml` from the target branch.\n\nIt uses this to decide which CI and which checks need to be run, and collects information\nabout the CI request.\n\nThis can be configured on a per-branch basis, by editing the file on the branch.\n\nThis also holds the authoritative build image information.\n\nUsers can request a CI run in a PR with custom build images by editing the config.yml file\non the relevant branch. CI will allow this but flag the change.\n\nLikewise the version is checked at this stage, and CI flags if it has changed.\n\nNo other CI vars should be editable by users in a PR.\n\n#### CI check runs *on main* listen for incoming requests and run if required:\n\nThese checks *always* run on `main` but with the repo checked out for the branch or the PR.\n\nIf branches require custom CI this can be added in the relevant file *on main* with\na condition to only trigger for relevant target branch.\n\n#### Checks are completed at the end of each CI run:\n\nCurrently this reports only on the overall outcome of the CI run and updates the check.\n\nWe can add eg Slack reporting here to notify on failed `main` runs.\n\n#### Retesting\n\nPR CI can be retested by issuing `/retest` on the PR.\n\nThis finds the checks related to the latest request and restarts them if they are\nfailed or cancelled.\n\nLinks on the request page link to the original checks, but the checks themselves will\noffer a `reload` button to refresh to the latest version.\n\n## Branch CI\n\nAll CI is run on `main` - branch CI included.\n\nThe CI will checkout the correct commits and run the CI at that point.\n\nThis means that the CI on `main` should always be able to run the current supported branches.\n\nThere are possible workaround for custom branch CI but the better path is to ensure legacy support\nin current `main` or backport any required changes.\n\n## CI caching\n\nCurrently only x86 Docker images are cached.\n\nGithub has a hard per-repo limit of 10GB cache for CI which is LRU cycled when exceeded.\n\nThis should just be enough to store x86 and arm Docker images for most of our release branches\nbut will not leave anything to spare.\n\nWe can probably set up a bucket cache for bazel and other caching but this will need to be\ndone separately for un/trusted CI.\n\n### Cache mutex\n\nDue to shortcomings in Github's concurrency algorithm we are using a mutex lock that\nis currently stored in the (private) https://github.com/envoyproxy/ci-mutex repository.\n\nThe lock allows CI jobs to wait while the cache is being primed rather than all jobs attempting\nto prime the cache simultaneously.\n\n## Development, testing and CI\n\nAny Github workflows that use the repository context (`pull_request_target`, `workflow_run`, etc)\n**are not tested in Pull Requests**\n\nThis means that changes to CI must be tested/verified in the (private) staging repository.\n\n### CI enabling vars\n\nThe CI workflows and actions are receptive to certain environment variables being set.\n\n`ENVOY_CI`: this allows CI to run in non-`envoyproxy/envoy` repos\n`ENVOY_MOBILE_CI`: this allows mobile CI to be run in non-`envoyproxy/envoy` repos\n`ENVOY_MACOS_CI`: this allows macOS CI to be run in non-`envoyproxy/envoy` repos\n`ENVOY_WINDOWS_CI`: this allows Windows CI to be run in non-`envoyproxy/envoy` repos\n\nWith these flags activated the CI runs will respect the normal conditions for running.\n\n### CI override vars\n\nThe CI workflows will also trigger for specific run settings.\n\nFor example:\n\n`ENVOY_CI_RUN_MOBILE_ANDROID` would trigger the android CI irrespective of files changed, etc.\n\nThese correspond to the run names as configured in config.yml - for example:\n\n`ENVOY_CI_RUN_BUILD_MACOS` would ensure the `build-macos` run is triggered.\n\n### Debugging CI\n\nSetting `CI_DEBUG` will provide a large amount of runtime information.\n\nGenerally this does not want to be set in a production context.\n","numLines":199,"startLine":1,"totalLines":199}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_012zASL1bUWEzrnx3s8zoZhA","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_011eMb7hJCZwm8e3woXhzHw6","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/onboarding.md","content":"# Envoy Contributor Guide\n\nA comprehensive guide to contributing to the Envoy proxy project, covering build prerequisites, build system, testing, CI pipeline, and code review workflows.\n\n## 1. Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Requirements\n\nBefore you can build Envoy, install the following tools and dependencies:\n\n#### Essential Tools\n- **Bazel/Bazelisk**: Envoy uses Bazel as its build system. It's recommended to use [Bazelisk](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk) to avoid Bazel compatibility issues.\n  - Linux: `sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\") && sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel`\n  - macOS: `brew install bazelisk`\n  - Windows: Download from GitHub releases and add to PATH\n\n- **Clang 14 or GCC 9+**: Required compiler\n  - Clang is preferred for CI (Clang 14 is the standard)\n  - GCC 9 or later also works\n  - C++17 support is required\n\n#### Platform-Specific Dependencies\n\n**Ubuntu (Focal 20.04 or later)**:\n```bash\nsudo apt-get install \\\n  autoconf \\\n  curl \\\n  libtool \\\n  patch \\\n  python3-pip \\\n  unzip \\\n  virtualenv\n```\n\n**Fedora**:\n```bash\ndnf install \\\n  aspell-en \\\n  libatomic \\\n  libstdc++ \\\n  libstdc++-static \\\n  libtool \\\n  lld \\\n  patch \\\n  python3-pip\n```\n\n**macOS**:\n```bash\nbrew install coreutils wget libtool go bazelisk clang-format autoconf aspell\n```\nNote: Xcode (full version, not just Command Line Tools) is required.\n\n**Windows 10/11**:\n- Visual Studio 2019 Build Tools (with VC++ workload)\n- MSYS2 bash shell\n- Python 3 (windows-native version from python.org, not MSYS2)\n- Windows SDK 1903+\n\n#### Optional but Recommended\n- **Docker**: For building with the same environment as CI\n- **buildifier**: For BUILD file formatting (`go install github.com/bazelbuild/buildtools/buildifier@latest`)\n- **addr2line**: For symbol resolution in stack traces\n\n### Documentation References\n- [Full Bazel setup documentation](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers)\n- [Envoy dependency policy](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/DEPENDENCY_POLICY.md)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Build System\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its build system. Bazel provides:\n- Declarative build configuration via `BUILD` files\n- Consistent builds across different machines\n- Remote execution support\n- Incremental builds with caching\n\n### Key Build Commands\n\n#### Building the Full Envoy Binary\n```bash\n# Development build (unoptimized, with debug symbols)\nbazel build //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Release/optimized build\nbazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Debug build (fully instrumented)\nbazel build -c dbg //source/exe:envoy-static\n\n# Shorter alias (recommended)\nbazel build envoy  # defaults to debug build\n```\n\n#### Building Specific Components\n```bash\n# Build a specific library\nbazel build //source/common/http:http_lib\n\n# Build a specific filter extension\nbazel build //source/extensions/filters/http/router:router_lib\n\n# Build a specific test\nbazel build //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n```\n\n#### Build Configuration Options\n- **-c opt**: Optimized release build\n- **-c dbg**: Debug build with full symbols\n- **--config=clang**: Use Clang compiler with libstdc++\n- **--config=libc++**: Use Clang with libc++ (for compatibility testing)\n- **--config=docker-clang**: Build in Docker sandbox (consistent environment)\n- **--config=remote-clang**: Use GCP RBE remote execution\n\n#### Running the Built Binary\n```bash\n# After building with: bazel build -c opt //source/exe:envoy-static\n$(bazel info bazel-genfiles)/source/exe/envoy-static --config-path /path/to/config.yaml\n```\n\n### Build Architecture\n\nThe repository is organized as follows:\n- **api/**: Protocol buffer definitions (data plane API)\n- **source/common/**: Core Envoy implementation\n- **source/extensions/**: Optional filter and extension implementations\n- **envoy/**: Public interface headers (mostly abstract classes)\n- **test/**: All test code (unit, integration, mocks)\n- **bazel/**: Build configuration and Bazel rules\n\n### Key Build Files\n- **WORKSPACE**: Bazel workspace configuration and external dependency management\n- **.bazelrc**: Bazel default build options\n- **BUILD**: Build target definitions (one per directory with source files)\n- **bazel/repositories.bzl**: External dependency versions\n- **bazel/envoy_build_system.bzl**: Custom Envoy Bazel rules\n\n### Custom Bazel Rules\nEnvoy defines custom build rules in `bazel/envoy_build_system.bzl`:\n- **envoy_cc_library**: C++ libraries\n- **envoy_cc_test**: C++ unit tests with Google Test\n- **envoy_cc_binary**: C++ executables\n- **envoy_cc_mock**: Mock implementations for testing\n- **envoy_cc_extension**: Filter extensions with metadata\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nEnvoy uses **Google Test** (gtest) and **Google Mock** for testing, organized into unit tests and integration tests.\n\n### Running All Tests\n```bash\n# Run all tests\nbazel test //test/...\n\n# Run all tests with verbose output\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/...\n```\n\n### Running Specific Tests\n```bash\n# Run a specific test file\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Run with streamed output (shows output in real-time)\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\n\n# Run with additional test arguments\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --test_arg=\"-l trace\"\n```\n\n### Test Environment Configuration\n\n#### IP Version Testing\nBy default, tests exercise both IPv4 and IPv6:\n```bash\n# IPv4 only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v4only\n\n# IPv6 only\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v6only\n```\n\n#### Memory Leak Detection\nTests use gperftools heap checker by default:\n```bash\n# Disable heap checker\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=\n\n# Use minimal mode (less strict)\nbazel test //test/... --test_env=HEAPCHECK=minimal\n```\n\n#### Force Test Re-run\n```bash\n# Bypass test result cache\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --cache_test_results=no\n```\n\n### Test Organization\n\n- **Unit tests**: Located in `test/` directories matching `source/` structure\n  - Example: `test/common/http/` tests code in `source/common/http/`\n- **Integration tests**: Located in `test/integration/`\n  - End-to-end tests with real server code and fake clients/upstreams\n- **Mocks**: Located in `test/mocks/`\n  - Mock implementations of all core interfaces\n- **Test utilities**: Located in `test/test_common/`\n  - Shared testing utilities and helpers\n\n### Test Frameworks and Tools\n\n**Google Test**: Unit testing framework\n- Macro-based tests: `TEST(TestClass, TestName) { ... }`\n- Test fixtures: `TEST_F(FixtureName, TestName) { ... }`\n- Assertions: `ASSERT_*` and `EXPECT_*` macros\n- Reference: https://github.com/google/googletest\n\n**Google Mock**: Mocking library\n- `EXPECT_CALL(mock, method()).Times(...).WillOnce(...)`\n- Matchers for flexible assertions\n- Envoy defines custom matchers in `test/test_common/test_macros.h`\n\n**Custom Matchers** (from test/README.md):\n- `HeaderValueOf()`: Check HTTP headers\n- `HttpStatusIs()`: Check HTTP status codes\n- `ProtoEq()` / `ProtoEqIgnoringField()`: Protobuf comparison\n- Reference: `test/README.md`\n\n### Test Coverage\n\nEnvoy requires **100% test coverage** for new code:\n```bash\n# Generate coverage report (requires coverage build)\nbazel test //test/... --config=coverage\n```\n\nIf 100% coverage is not possible, you must explain why in the PR description.\n\n### Debugging Tests\n\n#### Running Under GDB\n```bash\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test\nbazel build -c dbg //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test.dwp\ngdb bazel-bin/test/common/http/async_client_impl_test\n```\n\n#### Running in Sandbox\n```bash\n# Break out of sandbox (for running with local tools)\nbazel test //test/common/http:async_client_impl_test --strategy=TestRunner=local --run_under=/path/to/tool.sh\n```\n\n#### Stack Traces\n```bash\n# With symbol resolution\nbazel test -c dbg //test/server:backtrace_test \\\n  --run_under=//tools:stack_decode \\\n  --strategy=TestRunner=local \\\n  --cache_test_results=no \\\n  --test_output=all\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\nEnvoy uses **GitHub Actions workflows** for continuous integration, replacing the previous Azure Pipelines system.\n\n### CI Platform and Configuration\n\n**Platform**: GitHub Actions\n- **Configuration location**: `.github/workflows/` and `.github/config.yml`\n- **Build images**: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` Docker images\n- **Current image SHA**: Specified in `.github/config.yml` under `build-image.sha`\n\n### CI Workflow Structure\n\nCI is organized around a request-response model:\n- **request.yml**: Triggered by push/PR, triggers the main CI pipeline\n- **_request.yml**: Reusable workflow that reads config and initiates checks\n- **Check workflows**: Run on main branch but check out target branch/PR code\n\nThis design ensures:\n- All CI logic lives on main (prevents bad actors in PRs from modifying CI)\n- PRs can only change build image and version config\n- Consistent execution across all branches\n\n### Required Checks\n\nThe following checks must pass before merging (from `.github/config.yml`):\n\n1. **Build Checks** (check-build, check-coverage, check-san)\n   - `check-build`: Builds the project with standard configuration\n   - `check-coverage`: Verifies code coverage meets requirements\n   - `check-san`: Runs with sanitizers (AddressSanitizer, UndefinedBehaviorSanitizer)\n\n2. **Prechecks** (precheck-deps, precheck-format, precheck-publish)\n   - `precheck-format`: Code formatting (clang-format) and linting\n   - `precheck-deps`: Dependency validation\n   - `precheck-publish`: Documentation validation\n\n3. **macOS Build** (build-macos)\n   - Validates compilation on macOS\n\n4. **Publish and Verify**\n   - Verifies binary publishing and release artifacts\n\n### CI Commands and Retesting\n\n**Retesting a PR**:\n```bash\n# Comment on the PR:\n/retest\n```\n\n**Kicking CI with an empty commit**:\n```bash\n# Create alias in .gitconfig:\n[alias]\n    kick-ci = !\"git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\"\n\n# Then run:\ngit kick-ci\n```\n\n### Local CI Testing with Docker\n\nBuild and test locally using the same Docker image as CI:\n\n```bash\n# Development build\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Run specific CI tasks\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh clang_tidy'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n```\n\n### CI Build Images\n\n**Standard Linux Image** (`envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`):\n- Based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal)\n- GCC 9 and Clang 14 compilers\n- All required build dependencies\n- Current SHA in `.github/config.yml`\n\n**Using CI Docker Image Locally**:\n```bash\nexport IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n### Coverage Builds\n\n```bash\n# Generate coverage report\nbazel test //test/... --config=coverage\n\n# View coverage HTML report\n# Generated in bazel-out directory\n```\n\n### Typical CI Runtime\n\n- Full CI run: 30-60 minutes (depending on parallelization)\n- Building alone: 10-20 minutes\n- Testing: 20-40 minutes\n- Sanitizers (ASAN, UBSAN): Additional 10-15 minutes\n\n---\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Before You Start\n\n**Communicate early for major features**:\n- Major feature = >100 LOC or user-facing behavior changes\n- Open a GitHub issue to discuss before implementing\n- Prevents wasted effort and ensures design agreement\n\nReference: [CONTRIBUTING.md - Communication](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/CONTRIBUTING.md#communication)\n\n### PR Requirements\n\n**All PRs must satisfy**:\n1. ✅ All tests pass (both new and existing)\n2. ✅ 100% code coverage for new code\n3. ✅ Proper code formatting (clang-format)\n4. ✅ DCO sign-off on all commits\n5. ✅ Meaningful commit message\n6. ✅ Documentation updates (if user-facing)\n7. ✅ Release notes (if user-impacting)\n\n### Setting Up for Development\n\nInstall the development support toolchain:\n```bash\n./support/bootstrap\n```\n\nThis sets up Git hooks for:\n- Automatic DCO sign-off on commits\n- Pre-push format and DCO verification\n- Other development checks\n\nReference: [support/README.md](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/support/README.md)\n\n### Code Style and Standards\n\n**Coding Style**: See [STYLE.md](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/STYLE.md)\n\nKey points:\n- **Formatting**: Enforced by clang-format (auto-checked by CI)\n- **Language**: Follow [Google C++ Style Guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html) with Envoy-specific deviations\n- **Line limit**: 100 columns\n- **Naming**:\n  - Functions: `camelCase()` starting with lowercase\n  - Member variables: `_postfix` (e.g., `foo_`)\n  - Enum values: `PascalCase`\n  - Constants: `kConstantName` or `CONSTANT_NAME`\n- **Formatting tools**:\n  - clang-format: Automatic formatting\n  - clang-tidy: Linting (enforced .clang-tidy config)\n  - buildifier: BUILD file formatting\n\n**Inclusive Language Policy**:\n- ❌ Don't use: whitelist, blacklist, master, slave\n- ✅ Use instead: allowlist, denylist/blocklist, primary/main, secondary/replica\n\n### Inclusive Language Policy\n\nThe Envoy community requires inclusive language. Refer to [CONTRIBUTING.md - Inclusive Language Policy](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/CONTRIBUTING.md#inclusive-language-policy)\n\n### PR Submission Checklist\n\n1. **Create a fork** of the repository\n2. **Install git hooks**:\n   ```bash\n   ./support/bootstrap\n   ```\n3. **Create a feature branch**:\n   ```bash\n   git checkout -b my-feature-branch\n   ```\n4. **Make changes and add tests** (100% coverage required)\n5. **Format code**:\n   ```bash\n   bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n   bazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main -v warn\n   ```\n6. **Run tests locally**:\n   ```bash\n   bazel test //test/... --cache_test_results=no\n   ```\n7. **Commit with message**:\n   ```bash\n   git commit -s  # -s adds DCO sign-off\n   # Or configure aliases:\n   git config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\n   ```\n8. **Push and create PR**:\n   ```bash\n   git push origin my-feature-branch\n   ```\n\n### PR Title and Description Format\n\n**Title Format**:\n- Start with subsystem name in lowercase\n- Format: `subsystem: brief description`\n- Examples:\n  - `docs: fix grammar error`\n  - `http conn man: add new feature`\n  - `router: fix header forwarding bug`\n\n**Commit Message**:\n- Used as the final PR merge commit message\n- Should explain what and why (not just what)\n- For bug fixes: describe the issue and solution\n- For features: explain the feature and how to enable it\n\n**PR Description Template** (auto-filled):\n```\n## Title\n[PR title here]\n\n## Commit Message\n[Commit message - will be used as merge commit message]\n\n## Additional Description\n[Context useful to reviewers]\n\n## Risk Level\n[Low | Medium | High]\n\n## Testing\n[Describe testing performed]\n\n## Documentation\n[N/A | Description of docs changes]\n\n## Release Notes\n[N/A | Description for release notes in changelogs/current.yaml]\n\n## Related Issues\n[Fixes #XXX | Related to #XXX]\n```\n\n### Creating Release Notes\n\nFor user-impacting or extension-developer-impacting changes, add release notes:\n\n```bash\n# Edit changelogs/current.yaml\n# Add entry under relevant section (bug_fixes, major_features, etc.)\n```\n\n### Dealing with Review Feedback\n\n**During review**:\n- Don't rebase your PR (makes review difficult)\n- Instead, add new commits to address feedback\n- Reviewer can still see what changed\n\n```bash\n# After addressing feedback:\ngit add .\ngit commit -s\ngit push  # Just push, don't force push\n```\n\n**Before merging**, maintainers will squash/clean up the commit message.\n\n### DCO Sign-off\n\nAll commits must be signed off with the Developer Certificate of Origin:\n\n```bash\n# Automatic sign-off with git hooks (after ./support/bootstrap):\ngit commit -s\n\n# Or set up aliases:\ngit config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\ngit config --add alias.amend \"commit -s --amend\"\n\n# Then: git c ... and git amend\n```\n\nIf you forgot sign-off and need to fix it:\n```bash\n# Squash commits and force-push (only if pre-review):\ngit rebase -i HEAD~N  # squash commits\ngit commit --amend -s  # add sign-off\ngit push origin -f\n```\n\nReference: [CONTRIBUTING.md - DCO](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/CONTRIBUTING.md#dco-sign-your-work)\n\n### Review Policy\n\n**Timeline**:\n- Reviews typically turned around within one business day\n- PRs become stale after 7 days with no activity and may be closed\n\n**Reviewers**:\n- Listed in [OWNERS.md](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/OWNERS.md)\n- At least one senior maintainer for core code changes\n- Domain expert review required\n- For new features/extensions: at least one approval from different organization than author\n\n**High-Risk Changes**:\nMay require runtime guarding - discuss with reviewers.\nReference: [CONTRIBUTING.md - Runtime Guarding](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/CONTRIBUTING.md#runtime-guarding)\n\n---\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Scenario: Fix a Bug in HTTP Connection Manager Filter\n\nLet's walk through a concrete example: fixing a bug in how the HTTP connection manager handles certain headers.\n\n#### Step 1: Fork and Clone\n```bash\n# Fork on GitHub (web UI)\n\n# Clone your fork\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n\n# Add upstream remote\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy.git\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Set Up Development Environment\n```bash\n# Install development tools and git hooks\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# You can skip some hooks if you want\necho NO_VERIFY=1 >> .env\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Create a Feature Branch\n```bash\n# Make sure you're on main and up to date\ngit checkout main\ngit fetch upstream\ngit merge upstream/main\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b fix-http-header-handling\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Locate the Code to Change\n\nThe HTTP connection manager is in core code:\n```bash\n# Find the implementation\nfind source -name \"*http*conn*man*\" -type f | head -20\n\n# Key files:\n# - source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h\n# - source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n# - test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Make Changes and Write Tests\n\n```bash\n# Edit the implementation file(s)\nvim source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n\n# Add/update tests with 100% coverage\nvim test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n\n# Example test structure (using Google Test):\n# TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, MyNewFixTest) {\n#   // Setup\n#   // Execute\n#   // Assert\n# }\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Run Tests Locally\n```bash\n# Run just the affected tests\nbazel test //test/common/http:conn_manager_impl_test --cache_test_results=no\n\n# Or run with verbose output\nbazel test --test_output=streamed //test/common/http:conn_manager_impl_test\n\n# Run all HTTP tests to ensure no regression\nbazel test //test/common/http:* --cache_test_results=no\n\n# Run full test suite (takes longer)\nbazel test //test/... --cache_test_results=no\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Check Code Format\n```bash\n# Run formatting fixes\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\nbazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main -v warn\n\n# Or using Docker\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n```\n\n#### Step 8: Commit Your Changes\n```bash\n# Stage changes\ngit add source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\ngit add test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n\n# Commit with sign-off\ngit commit -s -m \"http conn man: fix header handling bug\n\nThe HTTP connection manager was not properly validating headers\nin the XXX scenario, causing requests with invalid headers to be\nprocessed incorrectly.\n\nThis fix adds proper validation of headers before processing,\nensuring requests with invalid headers are rejected as per the\nHTTP specification.\"\n\n# Or without message (will open editor):\ngit commit -s\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Push to Your Fork\n```bash\ngit push origin fix-http-header-handling\n```\n\n#### Step 10: Create Pull Request\n\nOn GitHub:\n1. Click \"Compare & pull request\"\n2. Fill in PR template:\n   - Title: `http conn man: fix header handling bug`\n   - Commit message: (already filled from commit)\n   - Description: Additional context\n   - Risk: `Low` (for simple bug fix)\n   - Testing: Describe your testing\n   - Documentation: `N/A`\n   - Release notes: Add to `changelogs/current.yaml` if user-facing\n\n#### Step 11: Wait for CI\n\n- GitHub Actions automatically runs all checks\n- Monitor the check status on the PR\n- CI typically takes 30-60 minutes\n\n#### Step 12: Address Review Feedback\n\n```bash\n# If reviewers request changes:\n\n# Make additional changes to implementation\nvim source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n\n# Add/update tests\nvim test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n\n# Test again\nbazel test //test/common/http:conn_manager_impl_test --cache_test_results=no\n\n# Format\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Commit (don't rebase!)\ngit commit -s -m \"Address review feedback: better error message\"\n\n# Push (don't force push)\ngit push origin fix-http-header-handling\n\n# CI will run again automatically\n```\n\n#### Step 13: Merge\n\nOnce all reviews are approved and CI is green:\n- A maintainer will merge your PR\n- They will squash your commits and clean up the message\n- Your commit will appear on main with a clean history\n\n```bash\n# After merge, update your local repo:\ngit checkout main\ngit fetch upstream\ngit merge upstream/main\ngit branch -d fix-http-header-handling  # Delete local branch\ngit push origin --delete fix-http-header-handling  # Delete remote branch\n```\n\n### Key Takeaways\n\n1. **Communicate early** for major features (open an issue first)\n2. **Write tests** with 100% coverage before/with your fix\n3. **Format locally** before pushing\n4. **Run CI tests** locally to catch issues early\n5. **Don't rebase** once in review - just push new commits\n6. **Follow the conventions** for commit messages and PR descriptions\n7. **Be responsive** to review feedback (PRs go stale after 7 days)\n8. **Sign off** all commits with DCO (`git commit -s`)\n\n### Additional Resources\n\n- **CONTRIBUTING.md**: Full contribution guidelines\n- **PULL_REQUESTS.md**: Detailed PR submission guide\n- **STYLE.md**: Code style and standards\n- **REPO_LAYOUT.md**: Repository structure\n- **OWNERS.md**: Maintainers for each area\n- **test/README.md**: Testing framework documentation\n- **test/integration/README.md**: Integration test framework\n\n---\n\n## Quick Reference\n\n### Most Common Commands\n\n```bash\n# Setup\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR-USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Development cycle\ngit checkout -b my-feature\n# ... make changes ...\nbazel test //test/... --cache_test_results=no\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\ngit commit -s\ngit push origin my-feature\n\n# Testing\nbazel test release build\n\n# CI Testing (Docker)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Format checking\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n```\n\n### Useful Links\n\n- **GitHub Repository**: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy\n- **Official Documentation**: https://www.envoyproxy.io/\n- **Slack Community**: https://envoyproxy.slack.com/\n- **Mailing Lists**: https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-dev\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Build Issues\n\n**\"Bazel command not found\"**\n- Install Bazelisk: See [Build Prerequisites](#build-prerequisites)\n\n**\"C++ compiler not found\"**\n- Install Clang 14 or GCC 9+\n- On Linux: Use prebuilt LLVM packages or package manager\n\n**\"Tests failing with permission denied\"**\n- May need to run tests with elevated privileges\n- Use: `tools/bazel-test-docker.sh <test-target>` for privileged tests\n\n### Test Issues\n\n**\"Test results from cache\"**\n- Use `--cache_test_results=no` to force re-run\n\n**\"Heap leak detected\"**\n- This is often false positives in debug mode\n- Use `--test_env=HEAPCHECK=` to disable\n\n**\"IPv6 tests failing\"**\n- Set `--test_env=ENVOY_IP_TEST_VERSIONS=v4only` if IPv6 unavailable\n\n### Formatting Issues\n\n**\"Format check failed in CI\"**\n- Run: `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n- Or in Docker: `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'`\n\n**\"DCO sign-off missing\"**\n- The pre-push hook should catch this\n- Or fix with: `git commit --amend -s`\n\n### CI Issues\n\n**\"PR stuck in CI\"**\n- Comment `/retest` to rerun failed checks\n- Or create empty commit: `git commit --allow-empty -m \"Kick CI\" && git push`\n\n**\"Need different build image\"**\n- Edit `.github/config.yml` in your PR (only allowed change in CI config)\n- Update `build-image.sha` to desired image hash\n\n---\n\n**Last updated**: March 2026\n**Document version**: Envoy
